### Post by gjoellee on 2009-06-30
_**The Joyful July 2009 Screenshot Thread**_

> * Stay within the board rules, no matter how hot you may believe the wallpaper/screen shot to be.
* If you are going to quote, there isn't a need to quote an img-embeded picture - Just don't do it. Please just reference the post by page number/page link/etc.
* Off Topic Posts will be edited or removed.
* The desktops thread is not to be used as a means to post explicit or suggestive, and provocative images (they must be safe for your kids and/or boss to see). Please help to keep the thread relevant and safe to browse for everyone.
* The moderators of this forum reserve the right to edit or remove your posts as necessary so they may comply with our Community Rule set.
* Please use reduced-size thumbnails, where possible, out of respect for people running on lower bandwidth or screen resolutions.
* To avoid having users having to ask you for them. we request that you format your posts in the following order:

Themes: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Wallpaper: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Icons: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).

Programs: Name/where you got it (with link would be nice).
Important Note: Any image posted that is over 800 x 600 will be removed! Use a thumbnail or use a text link to your image. If your image is removed, this is why.Wallpaper: Colors (from zixpk.com)
Plasma theme: Air
Resolution: 2560-x1024 (dual monitor)

Here is my KDEmod desktop for the first part of Joyful July. Clean and simple:
[IMG]http://ubuntuforums.org/attachment.php?attachmentid=119499&d=1246394856[/IMG]

### Post by Felliph3 on 2009-07-01
"Wow. How did you make the transparent panels? :smile: 		                   		  		  		 		 "

I did it in Compiz yes. Its pretty neat, adds a lot to the whole experience. It has a slight blur behind it, and its slightly transparent.

Compiz>Opacity,Brightness and Saturation plugin>Opacity> Then under windows hit new and add this

    name=gnome-panel | Tooltip | Menu | PopupMenu | DropdownMenu

with the value of 76.

Enjoy!

---

### Post by el mariachi on 2009-07-01
I have the pcf version... but it doesn't seem to work :S do I have to do ProggyTiny.pcf in the xdefaults?
```
<?xml version='1.0'?>
<!DOCTYPE fontconfig SYSTEM 'fonts.dtd'>
<fontconfig>
 <match target="font" >
  <edit mode="assign" name="rgba" >
   <const>rgb</const>
  </edit>
 </match>
 <match target="font" >
  <edit mode="assign" name="hinting" >
   <bool>false</bool>
  </edit>
 </match>
 <match target="font" >
  <edit mode="assign" name="hintstyle" >
   <const>hintnone</const>
  </edit>
 </match>
 <match target="pattern" >
  <edit mode="assign" name="autohint" >
   <bool>true</bool>
  </edit>
 </match>
 <dir>~/.fonts</dir>
 <match target="font" >
  <edit mode="assign" name="antialias" >
   <bool>true</bool>
  </edit>
 </match>
</fontconfig>
``` this is my fonts.conf

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-07-01
> **el mariachi said:**
> aah hehe sorry misunderstood :p

```
urxvt*font:xft:ProggyTinyTT
urxvt*boldFont:xft:ProggyTinyTT
urxvt*italicFont:xft:ProggyTinyTT
```

typing in just ProggyTiny won't work (the font isn't used) I need to use the 'TT' version. wonder why

so using just proggytiny doesn't work as well. Anyway assuming you moved your pcf fonts in your local .fonts folder, did you do mkfontdir, and mkfontscale, and followed by fc-cache -f -v after putting the fonts there? i have them in X11 fonts folder,and have the path defined in my xorg.conf. so xfontsel for instance can see them, and i use it in my Xdefaults, like here!

```

URxvt*font:              -*-proggytiny-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-iso8859-*
URxvt*boldFont:          -*-proggytiny-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-*-iso8859-*
```

---

### Post by BwackNinja on 2009-07-02
> **Nythain said:**
> what did you use to get the root menu/desktop menu in compiz?

compiz-deskmenu, disabled nautilus from showing the desktop in gconf-editor, added command0 in ccsm to be compiz-deskmenu, added in the desktop click plugin I have button2 with plugin "core" and action "run_command0_key"

### Post by BwackNinja on 2009-07-02
> **mjheagle8 said:**
> i love this. what wm are you running? and how did you make your desktop look like that? (i'm familiar with conky)

> **imnotthere said:**
> Which emerald theme is that?

I'm running compiz, and those aren't conky, but desktop widgets made in python, so I don't have to worry about doing extra work when I feel like changing my wallpaper. The lyrics widget currently supports mpd and rhythmbox, and that's an rss aggregator on the other side.

Emerald is custom
GTK is custom
Font is Lucida Sans 6.5
Menu is compiz-deskmenu

I can upload any of it on request. If nothing else, the taskbar is a good example of using libwnck in python.

---

### Post by BwackNinja on 2009-07-02
> **mjheagle8 said:**
> could you upload those please (the python programs)? also, would they work in openbox? do i need xcompmpgr running for them? i am very interested in seeing the code for them and learning how to do stuff like that myself.

They should work in openbox. Without xcompmgr, they won't have a transparent background, but they'll still work. Run them from a terminal first to make sure you have all the dependencies.

RSS_Agg_View.py, Lyrics_View.py, Taskbar.py are the three programs, the rest are just stuff they depend on.

### Post by Islington on 2009-07-03
> **easybake said:**
> Why are there min/max/close buttons on your panel?

to save space. this way when my windows are maximize I can hide the titlebar. and even when they are not there is a defined place to close/max/min them. its done with a panel applet.

### Post by MaxIBoy on 2009-07-03
na12, I'll give you fifty points on style, and negative twenty on readability. 



Due to an automatic update, cairo-dock now works without a hitch. This is actually why I'd split my upper panel in two: so I could add a dock between the two halves.

The icons are all custom but based on pre-existing icons (I just added the backgrounds and text.) In the case of the openoffice icon, I used inkscape's "trace bitmap" feature to generate an SVG, then I modified it by hand to remove most of the white "fringing." 

All zooming or other animations are disabled on the dock, and it contains only launchers (in other words, it is acting pretty much like a standard panel instead of a dock.) 


Screenshot is attached. If you want, I'll attach a tarball of the icons as well.

---

### Post by Zelandeth on 2009-07-03
Wallpaper on Screen0 is from [Rah-Bop on Deviantart](http://rah-bop.deviantart.com/) albeit slightly cropped due to zooming it to fill the screen, the curse of widescreen monitors - As for the one on screen 1 - not a clue - but I've been using it since 1998 at least!

The two monitors physically match up so that the join is almost exactly where it is on the screenshot to the millimetre - so working seamlessly between the two is brilliantly easy - though Compiz does sometimes throw a bit of a fit with the window snapping.  It can be fun to watch though...

Not much to say really!  Crux skin with a red colour scheme.  The second monitor tends to be occupied by Htop when I'm not actively using it.

Texture on the panels dates back to my Amiga days where I used to use it (in .IFF format of course!) as my directory window background.  Works pretty well I think.  Realised I should have got the Gimp out to do a proper capture so the semitransparent panel menus could be seen too.

Wireless monitor/notification icons have been relegated to the bottom panel because they've refused to stay put on the top one over the last few days and keep knocking my launchers for Htop and the terminal out of place...and I don't like things being untidy.

---

### Post by MaxIBoy on 2009-07-03
> **Zelandeth said:**
>  Wireless monitor/notification icons have been relegated to the bottom panel because they've refused to stay put on the top one over the last few days and keep knocking my launchers for Htop and the terminal out of place...and I don't like things being untidy.
I've had that happen in GNOME, if I went into fullscreen at a lower resolution than my normal operating screen resolution. For some reason, the panel felt a desire to resize itself to fit this new resolution, even though I wasn't seeing it. If there wasn't enough room on the panel for all the stuff at that point, things got shuffled around. I no longer had this problem after I upgraded to a newer version of GNOME.

---

### Post by Hilko on 2009-07-04
> **Felliph3 said:**
> "Wow. How did you make the transparent panels? :smile: 		                   		  		  		 		 "

I did it in Compiz yes. Its pretty neat, adds a lot to the whole experience. It has a slight blur behind it, and its slightly transparent.

Compiz>Opacity,Brightness and Saturation plugin>Opacity> Then under windows hit new and add this

    name=gnome-panel | Tooltip | Menu | PopupMenu | DropdownMenu

with the value of 76.

Enjoy!

Thanks a lot ! I've been researching for hours how to do this. This is exactly what i was looking for.
Thanks!

### Post by ajy0852 on 2009-07-05
> **perfectska04 said:**
> You can name them however you want, I just give them ridiculous names so I can better distinguish the folders!

Hmm is there anything like "Popdown" for GNOME? my right click menu is not particularly useful, other than quickly launching Appearance Preferences.

The icons and theme are great!

If you use Compiz, you can change the right-click action in CCSM:
General options -> Commands -> Set "command line 0" to the command you want, but don't configure a key/button for it there. You can but it will take over all your right-clicks, not just on the desktop.

Desktop -> Viewport Switcher plugin -> Desktop-Based Viewport Switching tab: set "Initiate Plugin Action" to "Button3". "Plugin for Initiate Action": set to "commands". "Action Name for Initiate": set to "run_command0_key".

I don't know if it's possible to change your right-click in straight Gnome, but Popdown and Compiz-Deskmenu will both work with these settings.

---

If you use Compiz, you can change the right-click action in CCSM:
General options -> Commands -> Set "command line 0" to the command you want, but don't configure a key/button for it there. You can but it will take over all your right-clicks, not just on the desktop.

Desktop -> Viewport Switcher plugin -> Desktop-Based Viewport Switching tab: set "Initiate Plugin Action" to "Button3". "Plugin for Initiate Action": set to "commands". "Action Name for Initiate": set to "run_command0_key".

I don't know if it's possible to change your right-click in straight Gnome, but Popdown and Compiz-Deskmenu will both work with these settings.

### Post by Nythain on 2009-07-06
> **cdwillis said:**
> Can you post the .Xdefaults for that shot? I like the colors you're using there :D
i changed a few since that shot, mainly made white actually why and black actually black, i think the rest are still in tact though
```

*foreground:#a0a0a0
*background:#1B1D1E
!black
*color0:    #000000
*color8:    #505354
!red
*color1:    #F92672
*color9:    #FF669D
!green
*color2:    #A6E22E
*color10:   #BEED5F
!yellow
*color3:    #FD971F
*color11:   #E6DB74
!blue
*color4:    #66D9EF
*color12:   #66D9EF
!magenta
*color5:    #9E6FFE
*color13:   #9E6FFE
!cyan
*color6:    rgb:87/ce/eb
*color14:   rgb:87/ce/eb
!white
*color7:    #F8F8F2
*color15:   #FFFFFF

```
there's the colors, mostly ripped off from other colorschemes, piecing together the colors i liked that went sort of well together, still a bit upset and blue and cyan being damn near the same

### Post by DK-420 on 2009-07-06
> **pataphysician said:**
> this is really great. can you provide details on what you're using?

I am using KDE 4.3 RC1

The wallpaper: [Win7 Wallpaper]("http://nyolc8.deviantart.com/art/Win7-wallpaper-113296831") - Unbranded version
The icon set is: [Titanium ]("http://gnome-look.org/content/show.php/Titanium?content=75038")
Application Launcher: [Daisy]("http://www.kde-look.org/content/show.php/Daisy?content=102077")

I set the cashew down the right side of the screen because having it on the top-right was looking too old.

Everything else is stock with KDE... The desktop theme is Elegance.

EDIT: Forgot to mention, that I am using the Daisy application launcher at the top of the screen.

I am trying to work on the Titanium icon theme myself since it really hasn't been touched in over a year as far as I know. I love this theme, and it looks awesome with KDE.

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-07-06
> **gymophett said:**
> I'm OpenBoxin'! :D

Can anyone help me find a better GTK theme for it? 
Thanksss. :)

If you are looking for a dark theme, then deviant is a good choice, although you should change the scrollbars and a whole lot of things to the colors of the OB theme. 

The Color me bad OB theme that you have there was ported to OB by Rydgel from my fluxbox theme of the same name. My intention then was to make a fluxbox theme to go with my Xdefaults, and not gtk theme in particular. But if i recall, I did use it with Rezlooks Infini Rose, I think. But it is a lighter theme. So it is up to you!

Another idea could be to change the window bar color to #222222 and the menubar background also to #222222 and use the OB theme with any of the Mire themes.

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-07-07
> **Nythain said:**
> Finally getting around to learning vim, and unified all the colors a bit towards thayers colors finally...
Window manager is Awesome
Colors are a modification of thayer's
irc client is weechat dev
vim colors i finally settled on desert256
font is DejaVu Sans Mono

looks great. that reminds me, you asked for my vim scheme right? i will upload them elsewhere and post the link here.

on a related note, the screen would be even better if you turned off the bold option. But the best way is to use a bitmap font, like terminus, or dina. I have had a pretty good experience setting up colors, and there are some setups which will look great only with bitmap fonts, and the others only with monospace ttf like dejavu mono and liberation mono etc. 

if you try something like terminus or dina, pixelsize>11, since your screen is big, i am sure they will look fantastic. my old eyes don't play nice with monospace ttf fonts anymore. so may be it is just a matter of preference.

---

How do you change the Gnome Menu button?

---

### Post by gymophett on 2009-07-08
> **fontis said:**
> How do you change the Gnome Menu button?
And what's the theme specs?

Right click the panel, click add to panel, scroll until you find "Main Menu", click it, and click add. You also might want to remove the other you had earlier.

GTK Theme: Black-Diamond(blue)
Icons: Simple
My Wallper: Aerostream, comes in all sizes and colors.

You should be able to find those on Gnome Look.

---

### Post by Sarai the Geek on 2009-07-08
> **gymophett said:**
> Right click the panel, click add to panel, scroll until you find "Main Menu", click it, and click add. You also might want to remove the other you had earlier.

I think the question was actually how to change the icon?

If so, it's located at /usr/share/icons/ICONTHEME/scalable/places/start-here.svg, where ICONTHEME is the icon theme you're currently using, i.e. gnome or human.

---

### Post by fontis on 2009-07-08
> **Sarai the Geek said:**

If so, it's located at /usr/share/icons/ICONTHEME/scalable/places/start-here.svg, where ICONTHEME is the icon theme you're currently using, i.e. gnome or human.

Yeah, changing the icon was what I meant. So I basically change the value in soem conf file or do I just replace an existing icon file?

### Post by Nythain on 2009-07-09

---

### Post by Sarai the Geek on 2009-07-09
> **fontis said:**
> Yeah, changing the icon was what I meant. So I basically change the value in soem conf file or do I just replace an existing icon file?

Yes, you need to replace the start-here.png or start-here.svg icon with the one of your choice. Remember to make a copy of the old icon in case you want to undo your changes. If you use an .svg (vector) image size doesn't matter (they're scalable) but if you use a png, the size you're going for is 24x24px.

---

### Post by Giant Speck on 2009-07-09
> **Sarai the Geek said:**
> Yes, you need to replace the start-here.png or start-here.svg icon with the one of your choice. Remember to make a copy of the old icon in case you want to undo your changes. If you use an .svg (vector) image size doesn't matter (they're scalable) but if you use a png, the size you're going for is 24x24px.

Normally, what I do is rename the old file "start-here-backup.png" so that I don't lose track of the original start here icon.

I think I have six or seven start-here-backup.pngs in my folder.  :P

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-07-09
> **Nythain said:**
> have you played around with Musca or Qtile at all? I've found i pretty much love Musca but its to tricky for the wife to use

i have had experience with them. Musca is pretty good. but somehow i feel more comfy with scrotwm. The default key bindings are ace, and damn simple and doesn't require any configuration. All i have in my config file are color attributes of the bar, borders, selected, unselected windows, and the bar font. Everything else is pretty much default, and it works fine.

Yeah, my girlfriend used to have problems with dwm as well. But whenever she visits, i change to fluxbox, which is easier for her to handle.

### Post by fela on 2009-07-10
Here's my desktop:

I added the tux myself btw with gimp. I used a layer mask.

It's very minimalistic but very powerful. What you can't see is that I have Gnome Do docky, autohidden. I also have Gnome globalmenu to save screen space. I also have as little icons (especially color) as possible on the panel, and I only have one panel. The reason I don't have any launchers is that I launch all my apps with my keyboard, using gnome do, which from my experience in all three major operating systems is the fastest ever way of launching apps. The OSX dock isn't half as good, and the windows start menu becomes nothing more than a silly joke. The other thing I like about my desktop is my icon theme (all black, something like that), it's _very_ minimalistic but it needs a few more icons to be complete, such as the amarok tray icon which really winds me up (I might make my own by modifying the original one).

---

---

### Post by perfectska04 on 2009-07-10
> **Tipped OuT said:**
> Hey, can you help me out with the album art cover on the bottom left side of your desktop. I can't seem to download it from the sources website. How did you get it?

Sure, you have to install subversion first to get it, though. Instructions from the site, I just added the subversion command:

```
sudo apt-get install subversion
mkdir -p ~/.gnome2/rhythmbox/plugins/
cd ~/.gnome2/rhythmbox/plugins/
svn co http://nedrebo.org/svn/rhythmbox/desktop-art
```

Then you just enable it in Rhythmbox > Edit > Plugins > Desktop Art.

---

### Post by Tipped OuT on 2009-07-10
> **perfectska04 said:**
> Sure, you have to install subversion first to get it, though. Instructions from the site, I just added the subversion command:

```
sudo apt-get install subversion
mkdir -p ~/.gnome2/rhythmbox/plugins/
cd ~/.gnome2/rhythmbox/plugins/
svn co http://nedrebo.org/svn/rhythmbox/desktop-art
```

Then you just enable it in Rhythmbox > Edit > Plugins > Desktop Art.

Thank you very much. :)

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-07-12
Thanks everyone. Here are the details.

Wallpaper: [Glow]("http://optiv-flatworms.deviantart.com/art/Glow-Simple-Wallpapers-128357725")
Plasma theme: Glassified
Colors: Just some colors that I put together.
Icons: Oxygen Refit Black with custom folder icons (attached)*.
Window decorations and widget style: Bespin
Fonts: Segoe Semibold and Y2k Neophyte for the clock.

> **izizzle said:**
> Can I get the details on the setup eightmillion? Also the Dekorator theme.

P.S: What do you use as a browser?

EDIT: What do have you shadow settings set to under System Settings > Desktop > "All Effects" Tab > Shadows ?

Thanks.

The window decorations are Bespin set to tiny with dots for buttons. My main browser is Opera 10 beta 1. It can be hard to find, but it's worth tracking down the Qt4 build. Here's my shadow settings:

[IMG]http://h.imagehost.org/0650/shadows.png[/IMG]

*Note: to change all the folder icons at once, I use a command like this from the icon root directory:
```
for i in 128 96 72 64 48 32 24 22 16;do convert -geometry ${i}x${i} -sharpen 0x.4 folder2.png ${i}x${i}/places/folder.png; convert -geometry ${i}x${i} -sharpen 0x.4 folder2.png ${i}x${i}/mimetypes/inode-directory.png;done
```

Edit: Almost forgot. The Amarok widget is a one off creation based off of [OtisBee's ThaSaver]("http://otisbee.deviantart.com/art/ThaSaver-88737957").

---

### Post by eightmillion on 2009-07-12
> **izizzle said:**
> Thanks a bunch for the help! The color scheme worked, but the top of the windows are still white, but in your screenshot they are not.

No problem. Bespin can be confusing. You have to change some settings in the Bespin config and not the window decorations config. Go to your style settings and click configure. From there, click on the KWin WM Deco page and change your settings to these:

[IMG]http://h.imagehost.org/0737/kwin.png[/IMG]

These settings don't take effect until you restart your applications.

### Post by perfectska04 on 2009-07-12
> **phynix said:**
> @perfectska04 - Posting that grey theme?

For the GTK, it's only shiki-colors with changed colors in Appearance Preferences:
Windows: #3c3c3c Text: #e6e6e6
Input Boxes: #474747 Text: #e6e6e6

For the icons, just checkout gnome-colors from SVN and read the README, basically - you just copy a text file with the desired color values to the gnome-colors/themes/ folder and the makefile will create a complete gnome-colors variation for the color-scheme you want (gray/black/white) for example.

This takes care of the dependencies and grabs a copy from SVN, you just have to read the "Theme Creation" part of the README and you're good to go:

```
sudo apt-get install subversion inkscape imagemagick
svn checkout http://gnome-colors.googlecode.com/svn/trunk/gnome-colors gnome-colors-read-only
```

---

### Post by Jimleko211 on 2009-07-13
This is mine.  Only problem I have is that my windows don't go over Gnome-do, so I have to keep it always hidden, even when no apps are fullscreen.  Any solutions to fix this?

---

### Post by perfectska04 on 2009-07-13
> **Jimleko211 said:**
> This is mine.  Only problem I have is that my windows don't go over Gnome-do, so I have to keep it always hidden, even when no apps are fullscreen.  Any solutions to fix this?

Try the "Intellihide" option. It hides when a focused application is overlapping the dock, and comes back when the application is unfocused or no application is near the dock.

---

### Post by Jimleko211 on 2009-07-13

### Post by Tibuda on 2009-07-13
[https://launchpad.net/~do-core/+archive/ppa](https://launchpad.net/~do-core/+archive/ppa)

> 64-bit users! There is a bug in Launchpad's ppa that causes 64-bit mono package builds to fail, but David was in the marines for 12 years and only learned one thing- Leave no man behind. This message doesn't apply to plugins, however. Plugins are architecture independent and build fine in the PPA. You should use plugins from the PPA, and for core we've got a package for you at [http://launchpad.net/do/+download](http://launchpad.net/do/+download)

---

### Post by dsavi on 2009-07-14

---

### Post by hellion0 on 2009-07-14
> **dsavi said:**
> ^ I've been trying to find out how to do that (No DE, no WM) all day... :P Can you or someone else tell me how?

I found all of the info I needed to make that desktop on [K.Mandla's blog](http://kmandla.wordpress.com/2009/05/24/howto-patch-and-set-up-screen-vs/). Best part is, I'm completely free from X on that laptop.

If you know how to get to one of the virtual consoles, switch to it, then after setting up screen, open screen in that console. Ctrl+a-Ctrl+S, Ctrl+a-Ctrl+V, and Ctrl+a-Ctrl+X to taste.

### Post by kk0sse54 on 2009-07-14
FreeBSD & AwesomeWM using shifty for dynamic tagging

Clean:

### Post by BabakSM on 2009-07-15
Only been using Ubuntu for a month so this may not be the most creative, but I think its attractive enough for my taste (while still being usable):
 
Theme: Emerald theme is Nova (I modified it to be more practical); max/min/close buttons come from Ubuntu Limited (I desaturated them first). Both of the original themes are available via search on gnome-look.org
 
Icon set: Oxygen Refit (white version). I also use KDE style icons for wireless because they're more attractive IMO than Gnome's boxy looking wireless icons. Both available via search  on gnome-look.org.  
 
Background: A shot of the Eiffel Tower by Anknara on Deviant Art [http://anknara.deviantart.com/art/eiffel-tower-75076445](http://anknara.deviantart.com/art/eiffel-tower-75076445)
 

 [[IMG]http://i684.photobucket.com/albums/vv207/BabakSM/th_Screenshot.png[/IMG]]("http://s684.photobucket.com/albums/vv207/BabakSM/?action=view&current=Screenshot.png")

### Post by mrdiego on 2009-07-15
> **Tipped OuT said:**
> Not a fan of the folder icons, or the cheap dock, but what's the GTK theme?? :D It looks great.

And I am not a fan of the Mac-like folders ... or better said those you see from the front like Oxygen, Hydroxygen, Meliae, Elementary, Gnome-Colors etc. haves ... If I am using Ubuntu (OS) I want have all their characters near to the original. And for be honestly I like more the folder-style what the org. Human-Set ships in. If I call my Set Humanoid so it should beware the main soul in it. And yes ... I know that not everybody likes the Human-folder-style. So Breathe for example is trying to import the Mac-style from the org. Human-folder-base. ;) A great pitty ... I miss the difference and the originality. :-/

Gnome-Do is a flat Dock. Okay. But it's a great and for me a very good looking Dock. It's a Dock for Gnome and not for Apple - so the Mac-OS haves it in 3D. I love the difference ... and not the copy 1:1!

my2cents
Cheers

### Post by raronson on 2009-07-16
Yeah, I agree with that sentiment in spirit.  I too would like to have a *default* desktop that's uniquely Ubuntu, but as polished as OS X.  I've never been a fan of the Windows look, but I see a lot of themes that are indistinguishable (or draw their inspiration) from Vista.  Yet, you won't see Windows and Mac users making themes that imitate Ubuntu (fringe exceptions aside)--because there's nothing spectular about the look of the default install.  Although, love it or hate it, the Human color scheme is at least unique--howbeit, it's draped over Gnome 2--which is reminiscient of Mac OS 9.

Hopefully Gnome 3 will be innovative and unique, thereby giving distributions based off of it a look that is distinctly identifiable as "Linux" (no matter the distro-specific branding).  Until then, *default* looks for Linux, outside of the various box-looks, will remain the poor cousin.

---

### Post by Pogeymanz on 2009-07-16
I agree. I find it sad that there are about 1000 Mac and Vista themes out there. I don't mean to step on any toes, but I like to see themes that are a little different than the ones you are forced to use on other operating systems!

### Post by perfectska04 on 2009-07-16
> **orion1315 said:**
> never figured that out lol
shouldnt it alrdy be in the repos?
and if u install ubuntu and then just install kde will it just be the same thing? idk my bars are all messed up and my internet and its weird when i use kde

I think kubuntu-desktop should install everything you need for KDE packages. If you're looking for a newer version than what is currently available in the repos, you may have to use a PPA or wait for the next distribution release. You should be able to choose wether you want to log-in to GNOME or KDE, so neither environment will be messed up.

You might see KDE apps in your GNOME menu-items and vice-versa, though - but it doesn't really matter. Both desktop environments have a very decent selection of applications, and trying out new things is always good.

### Post by Daisuke_Aramaki on 2009-07-16
> **izizzle said:**
> How would I download it? It is in the repos but I think it would just run on top of KDE. I want to be able to log into KDE/Kwin and then log solely into Openbox.

If you install OpenBox, I believe the session will be added automatically added to your login manager (kdm or gdm, whatever you use), So you can login directly into openbox. But i believe you could also login to KDE and use openbox as the wm instead of kwin, but i consider it ridiculous. 

If you are interested in openbox, check out [urukrama's website]("http://urukrama.wordpress.com/openbox-guide/"). there's a wealth of info on openbox there.

### Post by perfectska04 on 2009-07-18
> **boost3d23 said:**
> Got rid of Ubuntu 9.04 and went to Crunchbang 9.04. Still modifying it but this is what I have so far. Still have to get a dark icon set and change the wallpaper.

Crunchbang FTW!

Even someone as command-line challenged as me can use it without worries. If you want a dark icon set, you can rebuild your current ones from source and set a grayscale/aluminium color palette, it looks nice for me in really dark themes. The version on SVN also lets you choose separate colors for actions or devices, if you prefer everything not to be a single base color.

### Post by zehro on 2009-07-20
This is my current desktop. Finished it a few hours ago and intend to stick with it for a while. I posted a different desktop **[HERE]("http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=7639832&postcount=1487")** in the conkyForecast thread. That one was made while I was still getting my head around conky, but this is the final product of what I have learnt so far. 

Wallpaper can be found on deviant art:
**[lovelyart2104.deviantart.com/art/The-City-79146628?offset=40]("http://lovelyart2104.deviantart.com/art/The-City-79146628?offset=40")**

Gnome-Do Docky on the bottom (hidden).

The desktop has 6 instances of conky running:
-Time/date
-Song Playing (conkyRhythmbox)
-Small weather (conkyForecast)
-Large weather (conkyForecast)
-Rememberthemilk (conkyRTM)
-RSS

Conky Scripts can be found here:
[http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=7658655&postcount=8158](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=7658655&postcount=8158)

Fonts used:
- Futura LT Condensed
- Frakturika

I'd probably like to change the Docky Icons to fit them in with the desktop theme. I had played around with AWN and managed to put in some custom icons, but GnomeDo is just so much nicer to use. Maybe some new icons can be for a next release =)

Lastly thanks to the user Kaivalagi for use of his great python scripts.

---

---

### Post by zehro on 2009-07-20
> **londonali1010 said:**
> Yay! You found it!

GREAT screenie :) You know, if the Docky icons bug you, you can always just use Gnome-Do in normal mode, which is what I do. I don't have anything but Conky on my desktop now and I love it!

PS. Good to see someone into decorating their wallpaper, like I do :) It's a pain in the rear to change, though, which I do like every week!!!

Oh, tell me about it... ](*,) 

I was originally using one conky instance to place stuff all over the desktop. Had so many voffset, offset, alignr tags everywhere. Now i've split everything into seperate instances. Its a lot easier to position and move it all around.

I might have to re-upload soon. I really disliked the way the dock was fitting in with the desktop, I've since set it to auto-hide. It looked too much like it was just tacked on. I also set the mount drives to not be visible on the desktop. Its now a lot cleaner looking. I'm working on some extra tweaks and hiding stuff within the typography in the image.

### Post by narf41 on 2009-07-20
hmmm the soccer(ae)/football(be) match i´m watching is a little bit boring
so i used the first halftime: reworked the wall in gimp for a soft 3d look, made a simple nowplaying theme, customized the panel clock in gconf to a "Kalender" button (i don´t need two clocks hehe) and placed the calendar window with compiz (i don´t like the default look stucked up directly at panel and desk edge)

### Post by mrdiego on 2009-07-22
> **phynix said:**
> Theme details? I really like this one.

Thank you. :)

I like it simple. I put the theme and the icon-set in /usr/share/themes and /usr/share/icons; the metacity can stay local in your homefolder. Adjusting the panel a little bit and install Gnome-Do. That's all. Nothing more ... ;)

Here you get the exactly dates I have used:

[http://schollidesign.deviantart.com/art/Schollibuntu-D-105823432](http://schollidesign.deviantart.com/art/Schollibuntu-D-105823432)

All listed themes are pure quality and highly recommended by my side. The font is GE Inspira - a quality font too, but non-free. ;)

Enjoy ;)

### Post by narf41 on 2009-07-24
i just want to show new possibilitys with conky!! ( i don´t use it as default, it doesn´t match the other components...just a test :) )

the nowplaying is a collabo between conky and screenlet

cover and title/artist are drawn with screenlet
but background pc, the cover shadow (and the bar) are made with conky - yeah, conky allows now to use images!!! thx zehrothree for telling me

this is the only way to have a nice nowplaying background but a clean screen if music´s not playing (cause screenlet draws the bg images everytime, also if nothing´s playing)

[[img]http://ubuntu-pics.de/thumb/19790/conkyscreenlet_byAhJ4.png[/img]](http://ubuntu-pics.de/bild/19790/conkyscreenlet_byAhJ4.png)

### Post by ELD on 2009-07-24

### Post by ad_267 on 2009-07-24
> **ELD said:**
> Nothing fancy from me, ubuntu 9.04 64bit, newwave, disabled desktop effects made videos run really funny and i only wanted it for AWN patiently waiting for future version where compiz isn't needed (ati :(, going to go nvidia next time!!).

You don't have to use Compiz, you can enable compositing in metacity. And at the moment Nvidia works better, but I like the direction ATI is headed. Nvidia has no plans to support things like kernel mode setting, whereas ATI does and has open sourced their new drivers.

### Post by Subban on 2009-07-26
First time I have thrown up a shot of my desktop so please be kind :]

[[IMG]http://img193.imageshack.us/img193/6291/subbasshotgrey072609.th.png[/IMG]](http://img193.imageshack.us/my.php?image=subbasshotgrey072609.png)

Saw the wallpaper on a screenshot and it took me ages to find it, i'll post it here in case anyone else fancies it.

[[IMG]http://img193.imageshack.us/img193/7812/darkwoodx.th.jpg[/IMG]](http://img193.imageshack.us/my.php?image=darkwoodx.jpg)

The Conkyrc is pretty obviously a copied one, I did make a note of where it was from but can't find it now. I have tweaked it a little though, and it is attached, it uses VAG Rounded font (Volkswagon Group font, google it)

The playlist is Moc, a console mp3 player. Theme is tweaked by myself (attached sub.txt and lives in ~/moc/themes) to match the colours and probably should be used with my .Xdefaults (lives in ~/) for the colours to be right, I can't remember. I will include both. I use rxvt for the transparent consoles, it takes its settings from .Xdefaults but to make it fully borderless tell compiz not to draw title and borders on it or shadows :]

I also sometimes use XMMS and the matching skin for that is at [http://www.winamp.com/skins/details/185534](http://www.winamp.com/skins/details/185534) called Alpha Sport

Application, document and desktop fonts should be Aller. Window controls are Mythbuntu, Window border is Peace, icons are area 0.43.

I'm happy with it as is, I wish the Area icon set was more complete but you can't have everything, last time I tarted up my desktop it stayed on for months, have to see how long the legs on this one are :]

### Post by ajy0852 on 2009-07-26
Openbox with Gnome.
- Wallpaper: "Bamboo" from Interfacelift
- GTK: a slightly modified version of Neon from the "themes" section of the Murrine site
- Icons: KDE Oxygen icons. I also downloaded the OxygenRefit-Molecule icons from Gnome-look, and I set the KDE icons to depend on Oxygen-Refit. So even though it's a KDE icon set, the gaps get filled in well. I like the KDE folders better than the Oxygen-refit ones, the icons are crisper in general.
- Tint2 custom config, I've had it on the side for a while to conserve vertical space but it still just looks weird to me.
- Right-click menu is Popdown (now with a [link]("http://www.manatlan.com/page/popdown")).
- Oh, and a weather screenlet. I think that's all.

Edit: Yay! Post #1111!

---

### Post by twright on 2009-07-26
> **ajy0852 said:**
> Openbox with Gnome.
- Wallpaper: "Bamboo" from Interfacelift
- GTK: a slightly modified version of Neon from the "themes" section of the Murrine site
- Icons: KDE Oxygen icons. I also downloaded the OxygenRefit-Molecule icons from Gnome-look, and I set the KDE icons to depend on Oxygen-Refit. So even though it's a KDE icon set, the gaps get filled in well. I like the KDE folders better than the Oxygen-refit ones, the icons are crisper in general.
- Tint2 custom config, I've had it on the side for a while to conserve vertical space but it still just looks weird to me.

- Oh, and a weather screenlet. I think that's all.

### Post by narf41 on 2009-07-26
there are really no wp-fakes in this shots :)
all the images are drawn with the image-function of conky

3 conky scripts:
the first one draws the panel"extension" and the dark top frame of the sys info, including "sys" and battery bar
the second script draws the more transparent window with the sys-infos
the third one draws just the frame for the now playing screenlet, and if not playing, the small frame ("psst....", sshot2) (done with "if-else")

inspiration for the panel extension: [http://agarwal1.deviantart.com/art/MDRN-126702973](http://agarwal1.deviantart.com/art/MDRN-126702973)

the only suckin thing is to draw the images in gimp lol 

[[img]http://ubuntu-pics.de/thumb/20070/no1_dnOBmu.png[/img]](http://ubuntu-pics.de/bild/20070/no1_dnOBmu.png) [[img]http://ubuntu-pics.de/thumb/20071/no_n51ct2.png[/img]](http://ubuntu-pics.de/bild/20071/no_n51ct2.png)

---

### Post by JECHO on 2009-07-26
> **na12 said:**
> How you got frosted glass like terminal background?

ccsm > blur windows > blur filter: gaussian > gaussian radius: 8 > Alpha blur windows: class=Gnome-terminal

---

### Post by ajy0852 on 2009-07-27
> **sunexplodes said:**
> Out of curiosity, why openbox with Gnome? You're not using desktop icons, gnome-panel, or metacity, so what's the point of loading all the extra stuff when you could just use openbox solo?

Uhhh... uh... uhhhh.... OK, your point makes sense.

I was using straight up Gnome for a while, and got things set up the way I wanted. Gnome has some good tools for configuration, like the session manager (startup programs) and the theme selector. So basically I'm still using those tools, and haven't switched over to Openbox standalone. I have done that before, especially on my older computer but my laptop has plenty of memory, I really don't have to worry about it.

---

### Post by na12 on 2009-07-29
> **Chemical Imbalance said:**
> Would you mind posting your .conkyrc?

Mine needs a new coat of paint :D
conkyweather
```
# conky configuration
# edited by Mark Buck (Kaivalagi) <m_buck@hotmail.com>

# set to yes if you want Conky to be forked in the background
background no

# X font when Xft is disabled, you can pick one with program xfontsel
#font 5x7
#font 6x10
#font 7x13
#font 8x13
#font 9x15
#font *mintsmild.se*
#font -*-*-*-*-*-*-34-*-*-*-*-*-*-*

# Use Xft?
use_xft yes

# Xft font when Xft is enabled
xftfont nu:size=8

# Text alpha when using Xft
xftalpha 0.8

# Update interval in seconds
update_interval 1.0

# This is the number of times Conky will update before quitting.
# Set to zero to run forever.
total_run_times 0

# Create own window instead of using desktop (required in nautilus)
#own_window no

# Use double buffering (reduces flicker, may not work for everyone)
double_buffer yes

# Minimum size of text area
minimum_size 373 0
maximum_width 373

# Draw shades?
draw_shades no

# Draw outlines?
draw_outline no

# Draw borders around text
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders yes

# Stippled borders?
stippled_borders 8

# border margins
border_margin 4

# border width
border_width 1

# Default colors and also border colors
default_color grey
default_shade_color black
default_outline_color grey

# own window options
own_window		yes
own_window_transparent	yes
own_window_type		desktop
own_window_hints	undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager

# Text alignment, other possible values are commented
alignment top_left
#alignment top_right
#alignment bottom_left
#alignment bottom_right

# Gap between borders of screen and text
# same thing as passing -x at command line
gap_x 350
gap_y 0

# Subtract file system buffers from used memory?
no_buffers yes

# set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
uppercase no

# number of cpu samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
cpu_avg_samples 2

# number of net samples to average
# set to 1 to disable averaging
net_avg_samples 2

# Force UTF8? note that UTF8 support required XFT
override_utf8_locale yes

# Add spaces to keep things from moving about?  This only affects certain objects.
use_spacer right

# colours
color1 grey
# light blue
color2 6892C6
# orange
#E77320
color3 0968E6
# green
color4 78BF39
# red
color5 CC0000

text_buffer_size 2048

# variable is given either in format $variable or in ${variable}. Latter
# allows characters right after the variable and must be used in network
# stuff because of an argument

# stuff after 'TEXT' will be formatted on screen

TEXT
${image /home/dany/Desktop/conk.png}${execpi 1800 conkyForecast --location=SRXX0016 --template=/home/dany/weather-ob}

```

conkyrc
```
# Conky, a system monitor, based on torsmo
#
# Any original torsmo code is licensed under the BSD license
#
# All code written since the fork of torsmo is licensed under the GPL
#
# Please see COPYING for details
#
# Copyright (c) 2004, Hannu Saransaari and Lauri Hakkarainen
# Copyright (c) 2005-2007 Brenden Matthews, Philip Kovacs, et. al. (see AUTHORS)
# All rights reserved.
#
# This program is free software: you can redistribute it and/or modify
# it under the terms of the GNU General Public License as published by
# the Free Software Foundation, either version 3 of the License, or
# (at your option) any later version.
#
# This program is distributed in the hope that it will be useful,
# but WITHOUT ANY WARRANTY; without even the implied warranty of
# MERCHANTABILITY or FITNESS FOR A PARTICULAR PURPOSE.  See the
# GNU General Public License for more details.
# You should have received a copy of the GNU General Public License
# along with this program.  If not, see <http://www.gnu.org/licenses/>.
#
# $Id: conky.conf 1193 2008-06-21 20:37:58Z ngarofil $

background no
#font Snap.se:size=8
#xftfont Snap.se:size=8
font nu:size=8
use_xft yes
xftfont nu:size=8
xftalpha 1
update_interval 1.0
total_run_times 0
own_window yes
own_window_colour 000000
own_window_type desktop
own_window_transparent yes
own_window_hints undecorated,below,sticky,skip_taskbar,skip_pager
double_buffer yes
draw_shades no
draw_outline no
draw_borders no
draw_graph_borders no
minimum_size 200 5
maximum_width 200
default_color 8D3439
alignment top_left
gap_x 723
gap_y 0
color1 gray
no_buffers yes
cpu_avg_samples 2
override_utf8_locale no
uppercase no # set to yes if you want all text to be in uppercase
use_spacer no


TEXT
${image /home/dany/Desktop/con.png -p -3,0}CPU0 ${cpu cpu0}%  CPU1 ${cpu cpu1}%  
TEMP ${acpitemp}C  RAM ${memperc}%  
DOWN ${downspeed eth0}  UP ${upspeed eth0}  
GMAIL ${texeci 6000 perl ~/gmail.pl n}  PAC ${execi 1800 ~/newpm.sh}${exec head -n1 ~/.pacmanupdates.txt}${voffset -40}

```

weather-ob
```
${goto 90}Now ${goto 160}[--datatype=DW --startday=1 --shortweekday]${goto 220}[--datatype=DW --startday=2 --shortweekday]${goto 285}[--datatype=DW --startday=3 --shortweekday]${goto 347}[--datatype=DW --startday=4 --shortweekday]
${goto 85}${font ConkyWeather:size=20}[--datatype=WF]${goto 140}  [--datatype=WF --startday=1 --endday=4 --spaces=5]${font ProFont:size=6}
${goto 85}[--datatype=HT --hideunits --centeredwidth=3]/[--datatype=LT --hideunits --centeredwidth=3]${goto 152}[--datatype=HT --startday=1 --hideunits --centeredwidth=0]/[--datatype=LT --startday=1 --hideunits --centeredwidth=3]${goto 213}[--datatype=HT --startday=2 --hideunits --centeredwidth=3]/[--datatype=LT --startday=2 --hideunits --centeredwidth=3]${goto 276}[--datatype=HT --startday=3 --hideunits --centeredwidth=3]/[--datatype=LT --startday=3 --hideunits --centeredwidth=3]${goto 338}[--datatype=HT --startday=4 --hideunits --centeredwidth=3]/[--datatype=LT --startday=4 --hideunits --centeredwidth=3]
```

conky.sh
```
#!/bin/bash
sleep 10
conky -c ~/.conkyweather &
sleep 10
conky -c ~/.conkyrc &
exit 0

```

this is for 1280x800 display,I attached needed pictures

### Post by altonbr on 2009-07-31
Ubuntu 9.04 / Jaunty: Desktop busy, desktop wallpaper.

_Wallpaper_
```
sudo aptitude install gnome-backgrounds
```_Themes_ / [https://launchpad.net/~bisigi/+archive/ppa]("https://launchpad.net/%7Ebisigi/+archive/ppa")
```
echo 'deb http://ppa.launchpad.net/bisigi/ppa/ubuntu jaunty main' | sudo tee -a /etc/apt/sources.list.d/launchpad.list 
sudo apt-key adv --recv-keys --keyserver keyserver.ubuntu.com 1781bd45c4c3275a34bb6aec6e871c4a881574de
sudo aptitude update ; sudo aptitude install showtime-theme \
balanzan-theme \
infinity-theme \
wild-shine-theme \
exotic-theme \
tropical-theme \
bamboo-zen-theme \
ubuntu-sunrise-theme \
aquadreams-theme
```_Chromium Browser_ / [https://launchpad.net/~chromium-daily/+archive/ppa]("https://launchpad.net/%7Echromium-daily/+archive/ppa")
```
echo 'deb http://ppa.launchpad.net/chromium-daily/ppa/ubuntu jaunty main' | sudo tee -a /etc/apt/sources.list.d/launchpad.list 
sudo apt-key adv --recv-keys --keyserver keyserver.ubuntu.com fbef0d696de1c72ba5a835fe5a9bf3bb4e5e17b5
sudo aptitude update ; sudo aptitude install chromium-browser
```_VirtualBox_ / [http://www.virtualbox.org/wiki/Linux_Downloads](http://www.virtualbox.org/wiki/Linux_Downloads) 
```
echo 'deb http://download.virtualbox.org/virtualbox/debian jaunty non-free' | sudo tee /etc/apt/sources.list.d/virtualbox.list
wget -q http://download.virtualbox.org/virtualbox/debian/sun_vbox.asc -O- | sudo apt-key add -
sudo aptitude update ; sudo aptitude install virtualbox-3.0
```[U]
Wine[/U] / [https://launchpad.net/~ubuntu-wine/+archive/ppa]("https://launchpad.net/%7Eubuntu-wine/+archive/ppa")
```
echo 'deb http://ppa.launchpad.net/ubuntu-wine/ppa/ubuntu jaunty main' | sudo tee -a /etc/apt/sources.list.d/launchpad.list 
sudo apt-key adv --recv-keys --keyserver keyserver.ubuntu.com 883e8688397576b6c509df495a9a06aef9cb8db0
sudo aptitude update ; sudo aptitude install wine
```

### Post by RiceMonster on 2009-07-31
> **hoagie said:**
> I would really like to have the toad too. Also how did you get multiple terminal sessions in one big window?

He's using a tiling window manager, which dynamically resizes all your windows so they won't overlap and will take full advantage of your screenspace. He's using scrotwm. Some other popular tiling wms are dwm, wmii, awesome, and Xmonad.

### Post by easybake on 2009-07-31
> **hoagie said:**
> ... Also how did you get multiple terminal sessions in one big window?

If you are interested in getting multiple terminals in one single window just install Terminator. ```
sudo apt-get install terminator
``` It's definitely worth checking out if you run more than one terminal often.

---

### Post by yabbadabbadont on 2009-07-31
> **altonbr said:**
> @yabbadabbadont

I really like your icons from [http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=7709294&postcount=1238](http://ubuntuforums.org/showpost.php?p=7709294&postcount=1238), where can I get them?

You have to create them using the gnome-colors source package and customizing it.  Download the source package and extract it.  Then install imagemagick and inkscape.  (Installing inkscape pulled in imagemagick for me because recommended software is automatically selected by default)  You will also need to have the "make" package installed.  (I think it might be included by the default install)

Once all that is done, create a file in the "themes" subdirectory that was created when you extracted the gnome-colors source package.  I called mine "gnome-wisened".  (an older and darker version of gnome-wise ;))

Here are the contents of my file: ```
Name=GNOME-Wisened
LightFolderBase=#00ab55
LightBase=#00A150
MediumBase=#007339
DarkStroke=#004d26
```

Then, in the base directory of the gnome-colors source, run "make user-install-gnome-wisened" and your custom icon theme will be built and installed into your ~/.icons directory.  (replace the "gnome-wisened" with whatever you decided to call your custom theme file)

---
